  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3c8bb751-7fc0-4345-bcad-dffdda753bd2'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText17545422254512784769" style="display:none"><b>Made for Each Other?</b> <br />Betsy Ray has always thought that she and the fascinating Joe Willard would make the perfect couple. Now, in her senior year at Deep Valley High School, it looks as though she'll get her wish. As soon as Joe returns from his summer job in North Dakota, he's on the Rays' porch with sweet words for Betsy. It's going to be a wonderful senior year!<br /><br />Then Tony Markham, Betsy's longtime chum, comes calling -- and his intentions are definitely romantic. Betsy is torn. She really cares for Joe, but she doesn't want to hurt Tony. Can she figure out a way to follow her heart without ruining her friendship?</span>

<div id="review_3357492014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3357492014" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3357492014?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357492014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15698083387778621218">It has been such a boon to shelter-in-place with Betsy. When the real world got a bit too much, what a joy and relief to find shelter in Deep Valley and share in Betsy’s mostly -jubilant (albeit occasionally-turbulent) senior year. <br/><br/>I do rather wonder what it would have been like to read this in some suspense as to which boy Betsy goes with in the end – I’ve known all along thanks to some unfortunate spoilers but I think if I’d read this in my early teens, without spoilers, I would have been on p</span>
  <span id="freeText15698083387778621218" style="display:none">It has been such a boon to shelter-in-place with Betsy. When the real world got a bit too much, what a joy and relief to find shelter in Deep Valley and share in Betsy’s mostly -jubilant (albeit occasionally-turbulent) senior year. <br /><br />I do rather wonder what it would have been like to read this in some suspense as to which boy Betsy goes with in the end – I’ve known all along thanks to some unfortunate spoilers but I think if I’d read this in my early teens, without spoilers, I would have been on pins and needles. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Though I suppose the title of this book is rather a giveaway ;-) In some moods, my youthful self would have been a bit of a shipper and been on Margaret’s side for Team Tony. (Even now, I’ve had a special place in my heart for him all throughout the series, and I wanted to give him a big motherly hug at the end of this. Though my adult self knew he wasn’t the right match for Betsy, I came the closest I’ve been to being miffed at her over the Tony ordeal; I appreciated her noble goal, but not her approach. How relieved I was that she learned her lesson and that Tony didn’t go to the devil.) However, Joe is clearly so right for Betsy and it was lovely watching their relationship develop – I especially loved their Christmas gifts to one another, and their last Essay Contest. Young Me would have found much to admire in Joe and I would have felt that kindred spirit bond over a love of writing that he and Betsy share. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As ever, I love MHL’s depictions of the Ray family, Betsy’s friends (even if Betsy’s relationship didn’t surprise me, I had a big surprise about one of her friend’s!) and the town of Deep Valley. MHL is wonderfully perceptive about people, yet also so warm and kind about humanity. She’s never judgey. There’s such a sense of goodness in these people, even though they are never goody-goody. <br /><br /><br />Betsy matures even more in this book. I especially appreciate the way she is sensitive to how big sister Julia’s leaving the nest affects the family -- the way that she tries, not to fill Julia’s place, but to keep alive some of the little joys that Julia brought to the family or in bracing up and thinking of bringing joy to others on their first Christmas without Julia. <br /><br />“She knew she had helped the family, and as a matter of fact, she had been happy. That, she realized, was because she had stopped thinking about herself. <br />‘I’ve heard all my life that that’s the way it works. Papa is always thinking about other people and he’s always happy. I’ve got to stop thinking about myself so much—about how I look, how I’m impressing someone, whether I’m popular or not. I’ve got to start thinking about other people, all the people I met.’” <br /><br />This made me think of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29496453.The_Book_of_Joy_Lasting_Happiness_in_a_Changing_World" title="The Book of Joy Lasting Happiness in a Changing World by Dalai Lama XIV" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of Joy: Lasting Happiness in a Changing World</a><br /><br />And, speaking of joy, what a joy it was to watch Betsy graduate and look toward The Great World.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15698083387778621218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_6008711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6008711" />
    <a title="Melody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/369112-melody"><img alt="Melody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291050708p2/369112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6008711?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melody" href="/user/show/369112-melody">Melody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690133783" href="/book/show/6758030-betsy-and-joe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369112-melody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369112-melody?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6008711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1588685894974681438">8/2015 stet<br/><br/>9/2012 There's so much depth in Lovelace's books, so much backstory that's more felt than expressed. It somehow puts me in mind of Tolkien that way. It's the feeling one gets whilst reading a book that is entirely grounded in one specific world, the history of which is fully known to the author and intuited by the reader. It makes for a roundness, a fullness that satisfies in ways the less well-built world fails to do. <br/><br/>It doesn't hurt that, in my copy of this, tucked into the page des</span>
  <span id="freeText1588685894974681438" style="display:none">8/2015 stet<br /><br />9/2012 There's so much depth in Lovelace's books, so much backstory that's more felt than expressed. It somehow puts me in mind of Tolkien that way. It's the feeling one gets whilst reading a book that is entirely grounded in one specific world, the history of which is fully known to the author and intuited by the reader. It makes for a roundness, a fullness that satisfies in ways the less well-built world fails to do. <br /><br />It doesn't hurt that, in my copy of this, tucked into the page describing Betsy's Class Day photos is a copy of Maud's Class Day photo, and lo! she is wearing Betsy's outfit.<br /><br />Can't recommend this series highly enough. <br /><br />12/2009 Finally, it seems that Betsy and Joe will be together. This can't possibly be a spoiler, can it, given the title of the book? But the course of true love never did... you know.<br /><br />Tony (who I adore) comes into his own as a character in this book. We get a glimpse of the boy hiding behind the lazily efficient coffee-maker, the sleepily joking clown. And I wish I didn't know about the real-life Tony, because my fictional Tony goes on to have a long and gloriously satisfying life.<br /><br />Betsy's maturation continues, and she honors her family, her writing, and her friends- but she's still not able to say the things which need to be said where love and romance are concerned. Miss Bangeter teaches her famous Shakespeare class to the DV seniors- and oh, how I wish I could have audited it. I'm guessing that 90% of what I knew of Shakespeare in my teens came from Lovelace (and also Norma Johnstone's Tish books). <br /><br />A lovely end to the high school portion of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1588685894974681438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6847952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6847952" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6847952?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-female-author-or-illust">readbooks-female-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6847952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5431409503678273698">I love that the girls eat!!! There is no anorexia, no eating disorders.<br/><br/>I think that this book covering Betsy’s senior year of high school is my favorite of the 4 high school Betsy-Tacy books, this despite the fact that I generally detest love triangles in novels. I especially loathe them when, as here, there is a lack of communication between the people involved. I know the mores and constraints of the time didn’t permit Betsy to do as I most would have liked, but I do feel communication could h</span>
  <span id="freeText5431409503678273698" style="display:none">I love that the girls eat!!! There is no anorexia, no eating disorders.<br /><br />I think that this book covering Betsy’s senior year of high school is my favorite of the 4 high school Betsy-Tacy books, this despite the fact that I generally detest love triangles in novels. I especially loathe them when, as here, there is a lack of communication between the people involved. I know the mores and constraints of the time didn’t permit Betsy to do as I most would have liked, but I do feel communication could have been vastly improved. I admit that at times I was irritated with both Betsy and Joe.<br /><br />I love both Tony and Joe, although I admit I have basically rooted for Joe for Betsy. I do like my orphaned and quasi-orphaned characters!<br /><br />This book, as is typical of all the Betsy-Tacy books, is superbly written, and Lovelace is a gifted storyteller, one who’s brilliantly perceptive about following the main characters from ages 5 to 18; I can’t wait to read the next couple of books, and the companion books too.<br /><br />The Rays are a wonderful family. I would have sunk comfortably into these books and gotten much vicarious enjoyment had I read them as a girl. I think this book made me laugh and made me sadder and happier than any of the previous high school books.<br /><br />I want to know what happens with one particular character, but a Goodreads friend, one of those who introduced me to these books, says "It is a source of endless debate." So, now I am even more motivated to want to get together with other Betsy-Tacy fans and hear what they think. I have some ideas. I know what I wanted to happen but I guess it doesn’t, which is too bad.<br /><br />My public library has this book only in an edition combined with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7901.Betsy_Was_a_Junior__Betsy_Tacy___7_" title="Betsy Was a Junior (Betsy-Tacy, #7) by Maud Hart Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">Betsy Was a Junior</a> but I was able to get this edition from inter-library loan. I’ve already put <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7891.Betsy_and_the_Great_World__Betsy_Tacy___9_" title="Betsy and the Great World (Betsy-Tacy, #9) by Maud Hart Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">Betsy and the Great World</a> on reserve, a book my library does have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5431409503678273698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1990571614" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1990571614" />
    <a title="Beth Bonini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini"><img alt="Beth Bonini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444482564p2/3106785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1990571614?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Bonini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Bonini" href="/user/show/3106785-beth-bonini">Beth Bonini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=edwardian-era">edwardian-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3106785-beth-bonini?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1990571614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539627895317314056">No matter how well-written, I will only give a book a 5 star rating if I find it emotionally satisfying - if it intensely engages me on that level where I feel emotionally moved. This book! Oh, how very satisfying it is for those readers who have loved Betsy, and followed her development since she was first introduced at age 5 in Betsy-Tacy. Joe Willard - the hard-working orphan veiled in mystery - was first introduced in Heaven to Betsy, the book which chronicles Betsy's freshman year in high s</span>
  <span id="freeText8539627895317314056" style="display:none">No matter how well-written, I will only give a book a 5 star rating if I find it emotionally satisfying - if it intensely engages me on that level where I feel emotionally moved. This book! Oh, how very satisfying it is for those readers who have loved Betsy, and followed her development since she was first introduced at age 5 in Betsy-Tacy. Joe Willard - the hard-working orphan veiled in mystery - was first introduced in Heaven to Betsy, the book which chronicles Betsy's freshman year in high school. After various false starts, and tentative moves towards friendship, these two aspiring writers finally get their act together at the end of their senior year - and find not only love, but the kind of understanding and support that I think all of us yearn for in a relationship. This is a deeply romantic book, but romance of the best kind - because it is truly rooted in reality. Maud Hart Lovelace dedicated this book to her husband Delos, and she said that Delos was "Joe Willard to the life."<br /><br />The book is not just about Betsy and Joe, though; it is also about football, Shakespeare, theatre, growing-up ambitions, Tacy's first love, Tony's defection, Julia's trip to Europe and so much more. It's been a long time since my senior year in high school, but like Betsy, I felt quite overwhelmed by the complicated tangle of emotions that comes from realising you really are leaving one stage of life behind. <br /><br />"The older I get the more mixed up life seems. When you're little, it's all so plain. It's all laid out like a game ready to play. You think you know exactly how it's going to go. But things happen . . .".</span>
  <a data-text-id="8539627895317314056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers Who Enjoyed the First Seven Betsy-Tacy Books</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=young-adult-romance">young-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=vintage-girls">vintage-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=minnesota">minnesota</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3081263826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2764668308411749175">The eighth installment of Maud Hart Lovelace's wonderful <i>Betsy~Tacy</i> series, which follows the experiences of three girls growing up in Minnesota in the late nineteenth, and early twentieth centuries; and the fourth and final book dealing with their high school years, <u>Betsy and Joe</u> witnesses the long-expected commencement of a romance between Betsy Ray and Joe Willard. It also sees the poignant exit of a long-time member of "The Crowd," Tony Markham.<br/><br/>Senior year is always a time of changes, and Be</span>
  <span id="freeText2764668308411749175" style="display:none">The eighth installment of Maud Hart Lovelace's wonderful <i>Betsy~Tacy</i> series, which follows the experiences of three girls growing up in Minnesota in the late nineteenth, and early twentieth centuries; and the fourth and final book dealing with their high school years, <u>Betsy and Joe</u> witnesses the long-expected commencement of a romance between Betsy Ray and Joe Willard. It also sees the poignant exit of a long-time member of "The Crowd," Tony Markham.<br /><br />Senior year is always a time of changes, and Betsy, Tacy and Tib find that their final year at Deep Valley High School is no exception. Tacy, long the only girl in the Crowd with no interest in the opposite sex, finds herself with a most unexpected suitor! And Betsy, always of the belief that she can be friends with everybody, comes to the realization that she will have to make a choice: continue to string Tony along (albeit with the best of intentions), or tell him the truth about her feelings for Joe.<br /><br />Having never been involved in a love triangle myself, I have no way of knowing how I myself would behave (I suspect that I would opt for the brutal honesty that Betsy eschews), but as always, Lovelace makes me identify with her heroine, understand her choices, and sympathize with her feelings. I enjoyed this final high school adventures immensely, and look forward to accompanying the lovable Betsy out into the "Great World."</span>
  <a data-text-id="2764668308411749175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8083309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8083309" />
    <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy"><img alt="Carmen Maloy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195667618p2/563625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8083309?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen Maloy" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy">Carmen Maloy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8083309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16279955949833697912">Finally, love for Betsy! We've waited patiently and now we are rewarded with some romance between Betsy and the irresistable Joe Willard. Betsy Ray has always thought that she and the fascinating Joe Willard would make the perfect couple. Now, in her senior year at Deep Valley High School, it looks as though she'll get her wish. As soon as Joe returns from his summer job in North Dakota, he's on the Rays' porch with sweet words for Betsy. It's going to be a wonderful senior year!<br/><br/>Then Tony Markha</span>
  <span id="freeText16279955949833697912" style="display:none">Finally, love for Betsy! We've waited patiently and now we are rewarded with some romance between Betsy and the irresistable Joe Willard. Betsy Ray has always thought that she and the fascinating Joe Willard would make the perfect couple. Now, in her senior year at Deep Valley High School, it looks as though she'll get her wish. As soon as Joe returns from his summer job in North Dakota, he's on the Rays' porch with sweet words for Betsy. It's going to be a wonderful senior year!<br /><br />Then Tony Markham, Betsy's longtime chum, comes calling -- and his intentions are definitely romantic. Betsy is torn. She really cares for Joe, but she doesn't want to hurt Tony. She has to figure out a way to follow her heart without ruining her friendship with Tony.<br /><br />Betsy and Joe finally come together . . . and even then things don't always go smoothly! Full of tendeness and humor. Deep Valley at its best. <br /><br />The Betsy-Tacy books were highly autobiographical and Lovelace perfectly captures the innocence and magic of childhood. If you read this book and love it, please read the series. It will be books that you will never forget as long as you live. I also recommend the "Betsy-Tacy Companion" which is an amazing book that disects each book and compares it to it's real-life counterparts, including pictures of the "real" Betsy, Tacy, Tib and all the gang. <br /><br />I had the pleasure of visiting "Deep Valley" (aka Mankato, Minnesota) for a Betsy-Tacy convention back in 1996. It was incredible to step back in time and enter Betsy's world. We toured the city and I was actually able to step foot in "Tacy's" bedroom and sit on the famous bench at the top of the big hill. It was truly a life-altering experience. I have to thank my sister, Julie for introducting these books to me and changing my life. <br /><br />It's obvious how much these books mean to me. My first born child was named Tacy Kelly Maloy. Please read and enjoy. They are a treasure! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16279955949833697912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_79398826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79398826?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi-Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi-Marie" href="/user/show/921817-heidi-marie">Heidi-Marie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=2010-book-challenge">2010-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=2010-ya-book-challenge">2010-ya-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=ya-12-19">ya-12-19</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=2016-book-challenge">2016-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=own-in-the-home">own-in-the-home</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79398826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12132717817063362725">I love this book! Of course, I knew I would as soon as I met Joe, and that one of the books in the series had his name in the title. For much of the book I still found myself (like many others IN the book) thinking "about time!" and "perfect!" I was thrilled when things were going well, and angry when they weren't. I liked that both were at fault for the good and the bad. Of course, Betsy's immaturity and self-centeredness often had her putting more in the balance than Joe. Still, as in every bo</span>
  <span id="freeText12132717817063362725" style="display:none">I love this book! Of course, I knew I would as soon as I met Joe, and that one of the books in the series had his name in the title. For much of the book I still found myself (like many others IN the book) thinking "about time!" and "perfect!" I was thrilled when things were going well, and angry when they weren't. I liked that both were at fault for the good and the bad. Of course, Betsy's immaturity and self-centeredness often had her putting more in the balance than Joe. Still, as in every book, she learns some lessons and becomes a lot better for it.<br /><br />A wonderful book to read on a snowbound weekend because I had plenty of time to enjoy and not have to keep putting the book on hold as other things of life called for my attention. Plus, all the talk of winter in the book made me really feel like I was there. <br /><br />I missed Cab, but was glad he was here or there at times. I was surprised yet ecstatic about Mr. Kerr. If only I could be more like Tacy. (I think that with every book!) I liked that Betsy did a wink better in her studies than previously. (Still boggles my mind that some people don't put in more effort with school work and learning. Even when I didn't like the subject I made sure to do my best! Call me a nerd--I am!) I loved seeing how much Betsy really did grow up this year. Marked differences and realizations on her part. And one of the best endings that I couldn't have loved more!<br /><br />4/11/12 &amp; 4/12/12 Re-Read! I couldn't help it. It just sat looking up at me from my bookshelf. So tempting. And it promised to be much more interesting to my current (and sick) frame of mind than N.E.R.D.S. It was right. I skipped a few parts, but probably re-read at least 3/4 of the book. I think I am allowed to count that in my 2012 Book Challenge. In the category of "Classic" maybe? Ha ha. OK. I'll put it in "Other."<br /><br />2/4/16 - 2/5/16 Another Re-Read! I had to. I'd reached one of those horribly rare points of life when reading just wasn't appealing. None of the new stuff I was reading was intriguing me. So I pulled out what I know is a personal favorite to jump start my reading likes again. I think I only meant to read a few chapters. And finished it all within 24 hours. Totally worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12132717817063362725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_897593030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/897593030" />
    <a title="stormin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3809399-stormin"><img alt="stormin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/897593030?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="stormin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="stormin" href="/user/show/3809399-stormin">stormin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer897593030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12758892923286702864">So, this is definitely not the usual book that I read, but my wife insisted that I read this book and to tell the truth I'm quite glad that I did. See, I had just finished reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10079321.The_Magician_King__The_Magicians___2_' title='The Magician King (The Magicians, #2) by Lev Grossman' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Magician King</a> which had pretty seriously traumatized me, as far as book experiences go. (Read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878610249?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review</a> if you want more details on the nature of that trauma.)<br/><br/>After that: a delightfully upbeat and quaint story of high school romance and drama from the early 20th century was <em>just</em> what I needed to restore my faith in</span>
  <span id="freeText12758892923286702864" style="display:none">So, this is definitely not the usual book that I read, but my wife insisted that I read this book and to tell the truth I'm quite glad that I did. See, I had just finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10079321.The_Magician_King__The_Magicians___2_" title="The Magician King (The Magicians, #2) by Lev Grossman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Magician King</a> which had pretty seriously traumatized me, as far as book experiences go. (Read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878610249?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> if you want more details on the nature of that trauma.)<br /><br />After that: a delightfully upbeat and quaint story of high school romance and drama from the early 20th century was <em>just</em> what I needed to restore my faith in humanity!<br /><br />This book was incredibly charming and entirely delightful. I don't think it will bend the trajectory of my reading habits for years to come, but I am pretty sure that I will pick up at least one or two more volumes, although I may save them for particularly bad experiences. It's sort of like chocolate. Not what I want to eat for breakfast, lunch, and dinner but if you're recovering from a dementor attack there's nothing better.</span>

<div id="review_130632712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130632712" />
    <a title="Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1850370-lawrence"><img alt="Lawrence" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130632712?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lawrence" href="/user/show/1850370-lawrence">Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9781442015074" href="/book/show/8432912-betsy-and-joe">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130632712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9836194145626215716">I liked this book very much. It is the last of the Betsy "High School" books because the action takes place in The Crowd's senior year. During the year, Betsy becomes much more mature and reaches the edge of adulthood. <br/><br/>Betsy's relationship with Joe comes out into the open finally, but it is still not entirely smooth. I like the way that, all through these books, Mrs. Lovelace has described their frustrations, puzzlement, etc. as the two unknowingly orbit around each other. Betsy takes Joe on a q</span>
  <span id="freeText9836194145626215716" style="display:none">I liked this book very much. It is the last of the Betsy "High School" books because the action takes place in The Crowd's senior year. During the year, Betsy becomes much more mature and reaches the edge of adulthood. <br /><br />Betsy's relationship with Joe comes out into the open finally, but it is still not entirely smooth. I like the way that, all through these books, Mrs. Lovelace has described their frustrations, puzzlement, etc. as the two unknowingly orbit around each other. Betsy takes Joe on a quiet excursion: to see one of her favorite childhood places --- the tree avenue at the top of the "Big Hill" (which is also one of my favorite places in the books). This excursion is a far cry from Betsy's likely earlier ideas for fun activities. She has achieved enough self reflection to know that she has experiences, pleasures, etc. that she can choose to share and thereby reveal herself. <br /><br />Betsy also chooses to spend the spring vacation on her own at a farm where she endears herself to her hosts. She rises to meet their simple expectations that, of course, she will provide some pleasure for them in the way of music. <br /><br />Tacy remains a constant and, as usual, remains true to herself by falling for the guy that she, Tacy the individual, likes. He is an older guy, a working guy, and certainly not a person that members of The Crowd would once even have imagined to exist as a human. Tacy is really a very good friend and model for Betsy. Tib is still a bit of a cipher --- an antic and other-worldly creature. Perhaps, that is her function in the books --- to show that one's life can include persons whose background is entirely out of the ordinary. Unfortunately, Julia returns to attend Betsy's h.s. graduation and apparently for the whole summer. Julia is a suspicious, untrustworthy character in my mind --- highly driven, selfish, and a bad influence on Betsy. Her sway is made stronger by Mrs. Ray's obvious infatuation with her. Last, Betsy deals with her first death: the death of Mrs. Webb's adopted/foster son who had been B's correspondent from the Denver sanitarium.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9836194145626215716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1133524987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133524987" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1484380-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412727175p2/1484380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133524987?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/1484380-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1484380-liz?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133524987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14885454347038989482">Ok, I'm going to try—<i>try</i>—to pull myself together to get somewhat coherent thoughts down. I make no promises. <br/><br/>I was not expecting the angst that cropped up in the second half of this one. Which is a credit to Lovelace's narrative abilities. She sets the book up as we're used to: the frame work of Betsy's school year, the gatherings and holidays that mark each occasion; everything seems to be going well! And then the quarrel with Joe and how everything pans out with Tony and while the narrative st</span>
  <span id="freeText14885454347038989482" style="display:none">Ok, I'm going to try—<i>try</i>—to pull myself together to get somewhat coherent thoughts down. I make no promises. <br /><br />I was not expecting the angst that cropped up in the second half of this one. Which is a credit to Lovelace's narrative abilities. She sets the book up as we're used to: the frame work of Betsy's school year, the gatherings and holidays that mark each occasion; everything seems to be going well! And then the quarrel with Joe and how everything pans out with Tony and while the narrative still carries on its trademark tone, it is a bit muted. <br /><br />In the wake of this Betsy is at various times confused, sad, and determined to soldier on. It's here that we really see how much she's matured not only from those stories of her as a child, but from her previous years of HS. All together it presents a realistic conflict, handled deftly, that made me appreciate living in a time where a woman isn't caged by politeness in accepting dates. <br /><br />I loved the introduction of Mr. Kerr and the side plot of Tib and Betsy's concern for Tacy. Even from afar Julia's presence was felt nicely even if Betsy was trying to figure out how to fill the eldest sister role, learning that her role in the family is entirely unique. And, once more, the characters of the Crowd expands yet it still feels like a close knit group of friends. <br /><br />So many little things add up to a perfect whole really, but not much can top the deepening relationship between Betsy and Joe. It's been happening for several books and the ease of their friendship in the first half of the story reminds you of that. It also sets up some great tension; as a reader I was just waiting for them to declare they were together already! It gets messy and confusing, of course, but Betsy's recognition of her role in both Joe and Tony's lives, and the ending on the hill makes it all worth it. I loved the mirroring of their first meeting and then something they've never had: a picnic, Joe addressing that he knew Betsy understood where he was coming from and that "I wouldn't give a darn for my old Plan if you couldn't be in it." I actually cried. <br /><br />Really, about as close to perfection as you can get. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14885454347038989482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18322708895797576464">All of Shakespeare's heroines are essentially human. Somehow, it never fails to make me laugh. *g* <br/><br/>Lots of stuff going on in this one. I love Betsy and Joe. I'd forgotten how fantastic Joe is - he's right up there with Gilbert Blythe, in my mind. They are just so perfect together, and after four long years (for them *g*), it was wonderful seeing the start of their happy ending.<br/><br/>Tacy is quite interesting. I'd really love to see how other people read her and this storyline. The Harry romance is int</span>
  <span id="freeText18322708895797576464" style="display:none">All of Shakespeare's heroines are essentially human. Somehow, it never fails to make me laugh. *g* <br /><br />Lots of stuff going on in this one. I love Betsy and Joe. I'd forgotten how fantastic Joe is - he's right up there with Gilbert Blythe, in my mind. They are just so perfect together, and after four long years (for them *g*), it was wonderful seeing the start of their happy ending.<br /><br />Tacy is quite interesting. I'd really love to see how other people read her and this storyline. The Harry romance is intriguing to me, after four years of Tacy not liking boys. I'm not really sure how I'm meant to take it all - she had boys going after her, like Tom. She was comfortable with Tom and he pursued her, but she had no interest in dating at all. I think it's quite easy to see Tacy as a lesbian. But then along comes Harry and in one night, he's set her at ease, gotten her interested in dating and swept her off the market before she was ever really on it. So did she prefer an older man? Was she just waiting for the right man, Harry? Did he get under her skin and persuade her like he did Mr. Ray and the knitwear? Did she see him as the easiest road to the end she wanted, which was always to have children? It's kind of odd that Tacy didn't share any of her romance with Betsy. I know that she and Harry pop up in later books, but I don't remember in how much detail, so I can't wait to keep reading. *g* <br /><br />8-12-08</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12123892965391943380">The year is 1910. The place is Deep Valley, Minnesota. The person in question is the irrepressible, vivacious, creative, energetic Betsy Warrington Ray. In this book she is a senior in high school, her beloved older sister Julia is traveling in Europe, and her serious younger sister is soberly promising she will never be too old for dolls.<br/><br/>Betsy is enjoying the activities and chaos of her senior year of high school. <br/><br/>But she has problems. <br/><br/>Boy problems.<br/><br/>I was sorry Betsy was not more upfront with bo</span>
  <span id="freeText12123892965391943380" style="display:none">The year is 1910. The place is Deep Valley, Minnesota. The person in question is the irrepressible, vivacious, creative, energetic Betsy Warrington Ray. In this book she is a senior in high school, her beloved older sister Julia is traveling in Europe, and her serious younger sister is soberly promising she will never be too old for dolls.<br /><br />Betsy is enjoying the activities and chaos of her senior year of high school. <br /><br />But she has problems. <br /><br />Boy problems.<br /><br />I was sorry Betsy was not more upfront with both Tony and Joe. She has no malicious intentions but she ends up treating both of them unfairly. She is also a little oblivious to the tremendously luxury in which she and her sisters are growing up, even though some of the people around her (like Joe) are not as fortunate. <br /><br />At the end of the book she and Joe have a serious talk about the future. Joe asks Betsy what she intends to do:<br /><br />"Well, I was always sure I was going to be an author. I'm still sure of it. But I ought to begin selling my stories. I've been sending them out for almost a year now, and I don't even get a letter back. Just a printed slip that says they thank me for thinking of them."<br /><br />I am glad she remains sure, determined to find a way to open the closed doors in front of her.<br /><br />Of course I loved this book. It's an excellent, compelling, historically interesting novel. I am hooked on Maud Hart Lovelace.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12951619997372991302">It took me a while to find this one, but I finally read during my senior year two years ago. The title was promising-Betsy and Joe. Joe, not Tony. Not that I have a problem with Tony; he's cool and all, but we all know Betsy and Joe have always liked each other. Like the previous high school books, Betsy's world is centered around school, friends, boys, parties, the Essay con</span>
  <span id="freeText12951619997372991302" style="display:none">It took me a while to find this one, but I finally read during my senior year two years ago. The title was promising-Betsy and Joe. Joe, not Tony. Not that I have a problem with Tony; he's cool and all, but we all know Betsy and Joe have always liked each other. They're just like Anne and Gilbert Blythe: they are meant for each other, but it takes a while for it to actually happen. Like the previous high school books, Betsy's world is centered around school, friends, boys, parties, the Essay contest, and graduation. I really wish I was part of Betsy's crowd of friends; they know how to have a good time. Anyways, I think this is a good way to close up Betsy's school years and send her off into the Great World (with Joe).</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290841928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6444381957854860194">"You understand, I think, that I've always had a Plan for my life. In order to carry it out, I had to rule out girls, and I didn't mind. Even last fall, although I liked you a lot, I wouldn't let you come into Plan. But I've been doing a lot of thinking, Betsy. That Plan has been twisted about to let you in. You're in it, now, that's all. I wouldn't like it without you. I wouldn't give a darn for my old Plan if you couldn't be in it."<br/><br/>I want to have other things to say, but I really think I need </span>
  <span id="freeText6444381957854860194" style="display:none">"You understand, I think, that I've always had a Plan for my life. In order to carry it out, I had to rule out girls, and I didn't mind. Even last fall, although I liked you a lot, I wouldn't let you come into Plan. But I've been doing a lot of thinking, Betsy. That Plan has been twisted about to let you in. You're in it, now, that's all. I wouldn't like it without you. I wouldn't give a darn for my old Plan if you couldn't be in it."<br /><br />I want to have other things to say, but I really think I need to let this stand on its own. That is all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6444381957854860194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_249835074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249835074" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6414770-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558856149p2/6414770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249835074?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/6414770-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780780790919" href="/book/show/12389324-betsy-and-joe">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Classics, Children's, Fans of Little House on the Prairie, Fans of Anne of Green Gables</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Heather Vogel Frederick
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6414770-christine?shelf=read-for-book-club">read-for-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249835074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13419611857276153939">Oh, Betsy. I truly am worried about you. I did not like at all your behavior throughout this book so I think a more appropriate title would be <i> Betsy and Tony </i>. Oh Betsy! What went through your silly little frivolous head that seems to have been going crazy these past four years of high school. <br/><br/>Well, there's not really much to say besides that I hate how Betsy couldn't say no to Tony. Poor Joe! Betsy is just too much of a sucker for her Crowd! I was on edge and my heart was in knots the entire t</span>
  <span id="freeText13419611857276153939" style="display:none">Oh, Betsy. I truly am worried about you. I did not like at all your behavior throughout this book so I think a more appropriate title would be <i> Betsy and Tony </i>. Oh Betsy! What went through your silly little frivolous head that seems to have been going crazy these past four years of high school. <br /><br />Well, there's not really much to say besides that I hate how Betsy couldn't say no to Tony. Poor Joe! Betsy is just too much of a sucker for her Crowd! I was on edge and my heart was in knots the entire time she was with Tony. And that completely overshadowed any happiness I felt at the beginning about Betsy and Joe being together for a while, happy and romantic for ONCE. And then Tony had to destroy everything and Betsy acted like it was no big deal, so Joe was left feeling betrayed. Although I was mad at Joe at first, looking back I see that (as usual) Betsy was to blame. For the third time, oh Betsy! So sweet, yet so silly and stupid (occasionally).<br /><br />The part that I really loved about this book was the first pages of the book that talked about growing up.<br /><br />Quote 1: "...one was growing up so fast that one needed time to think, to correlate all the perplexing changes and try to understand them."<br /><br />I, myself, can definitely relate to this because I often find myself confused with all the different things happening in my life as I grow up, and I just wish that I could stop my life for a while and make sense of all thse "perplexing changes".<br /><br />Quote 2: "Betsy had clung to every phase of childhood as it passed. She always wanted to keep life from going forward too fast."<br /><br />This is me. Wholly and completely. Every little bit of childhood I am concious of, and of its passing. And, unlike most people, I don't ever want to grow up. Because I see already what I will miss, what I already am missing, about happy, blissful, naive times that I would trade everything I have now for. I am so scared of life moving forward too fast. Time is my worst enemy, which is why I sympathize with Betsy when she says things like this.<br /><br />Quote 3: " 'You grow older in spite of yourself,' Betsy thought resentfully..."<br /><br />In spite of yourself. Oh were words ever so true. I resent time and life when, in spite of what I want and need, I grow older. And I hate that. I just don't understand why life has to bring so much that ytou don't want. <br /><br />What's amazing to me is that, even back in a time when growing up didn't bring as many ocnsequences as our modern world, people still dealt with these problems and feelings, which at least makes me feel better knowing that it's not just being in the modern world that makes growing up harder. It always has been for people.<br /><br />Overall, this book was bittersweet. It was wonderful when Betsy and Joe got together, terrible when for much of the book she was with Tony breaking Joe's heart, and wonderful when Betsy and Joe reunited at the end. Looking back halfway through the last book, I feel like this book was more of a transition for me in the series than anything. Writing this review now, I definitely don't remember much about this book and don't particularly care for it. Nevertheless, I loved this book because it was still, nevertheless, a Betsy-Tacy book. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13419611857276153939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13720752958801194609">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br/><br/>Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankat</span>
  <span id="freeText13720752958801194609" style="display:none">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br /><br />Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankato’s center business district. The street, Center Street, dead-ended at one of the town’s many hills. When Maud was a few months old, the Hart family moved two blocks up the street to 333 Center. <br /><br />Shortly before Maud’s fifth birthday a “large merry Irish family" moved into the house directly across the street. Among its many children was a girl Maud’s age, Frances, nicknamed Bick, who was to be Maud’s best friend and the model for Tacy Kelly. <br /><br />Tib’s character was based on another playmate, Marjorie (Midge) Gerlach, who lived nearby in a large house designed by her architect father. Maud, Bick, and Midge became lifelong friends. Maud once stated that the three couldn’t have been closer if they’d been sisters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13720752958801194609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
